<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Caribbean</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Region to the east of Central America</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the group of islands. For the indigenous inhabitants of Caribbean a group of people  of Caribbean descent, see <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_people" title="Caribbean people">Caribbean people</a>. For the body of water surrounding them, see <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Caribbean_(disambiguation)" title="Caribbean (disambiguation)">Caribbean (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Time zones</th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%925" title="UTC−5">UTC−5</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%924" title="UTC−4">UTC−4</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Internet <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">TLD</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/List_of_Internet_top-level_domains" title="List of Internet top-level domains">Multiple</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Calling code</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/List_of_country_calling_codes" title="List of country calling codes">Multiple</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row">Largest cities</th><td class="infobox-data"><div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="text-align: center; font-size: 95%;">

margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Porlamar" title="Porlamar">Porlamar</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Cayenne" title="Cayenne">Cayenne</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Belize_City" title="Belize City">Belize City</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/UN_M49" title="UN M49">UN M49 code</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><code>029</code> – Caribbean<br/><code>419</code> – <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a><br/><code>019</code> – <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a><br/><code>001</code> – <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">World</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Caribbean</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>locally </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dce_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-dce-7">[5]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">El Caribe</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">la Caraïbe</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole_language" title="Haitian Creole language">Haitian Creole</a>: <i lang="ht">Karayib</i>; <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">De Caraïben</i>) is a region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a> that consists of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, its islands (some surrounded by the Caribbean Sea<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[6]</a></sup> and some bordering both the Caribbean Sea and the North Atlantic Ocean)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> and the surrounding coasts. The region is southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and the North American mainland, east of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, and north of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.
</p><p>Situated largely on the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a>, the region has more than 700 islands, <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reef" title="Reef">reefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a> (see the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caribbean_islands" title="List of Caribbean islands">list of Caribbean islands</a>). <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">Island arcs</a> delineate the eastern and northern edges of the Caribbean Sea:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brief_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-brief-10">[8]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> on the north and the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and the on the south and east (which includes the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Antilles" title="Leeward Antilles">Leeward Antilles</a>). They form the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Lucayan_Archipelago" title="Lucayan Archipelago">Lucayan Archipelago</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a>), which are considered to be part of the Caribbean despite not bordering the Caribbean Sea. On the mainland, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_region_of_Colombia" title="Caribbean region of Colombia">Caribbean region of Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cozumel" title="Cozumel">Cozumel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Island" title="Margarita Island">Margarita Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">the Guianas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guayana_Region,_Venezuela" title="Guayana Region, Venezuela">Guayana Region in Venezuela</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amap%C3%A1" title="Amapá">Amapá in Brazil</a>) are often included due to their <a href="/wiki/Political_geography" title="Political geography">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_geography" title="Cultural geography">cultural</a> ties with the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">Geopolitically</a>, the islands of the Caribbean (the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>) are often regarded as a region of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, though sometimes they are included in <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> or left as a region of their own.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> and are organized into 30 territories including <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_department_and_region" title="Overseas department and region">overseas departments</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependencies</a>. From December 15, 1954, to October 10, 2010, there was a country known as the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> composed of five states, all of which were <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> dependencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup>  From January 3, 1958, to May 31, 1962, there was also a short-lived political union called the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> composed of ten <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>-speaking Caribbean territories, all of which were then <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> dependencies. The <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a> continues to represent many of those nations.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_pronunciation">Etymology and pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The region takes its name from that of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>, an ethnic group present in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> and parts of adjacent South America at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish conquest of the Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>The two most prevalent pronunciations of "Caribbean" outside the Caribbean are <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ə-<span style="font-size:90%">BEE</span>-ən</i></a>), with the primary stress on the third syllable, and <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">kə-<span style="font-size:90%">RIB</span>-ee-ən</i></a>), with the stress on the second. Most authorities of the last century preferred the stress on the third syllable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> This is the older of the two pronunciations, but the stressed-second-syllable variant has been established for over 75 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> It has been suggested that speakers of <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> prefer <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ə-<span style="font-size:90%">BEE</span>-ən</i></a>) while North American speakers more typically use <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">kə-<span style="font-size:90%">RIB</span>-ee-ən</i></a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> but major American dictionaries and other sources list the stress on the third syllable as more common in <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a> too.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> According to the American version of Oxford Online Dictionaries, the stress on the second syllable is becoming more common in UK English and is increasingly considered "by some" to be more up to date and more "correct".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oed_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-oed-23">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Oxford Online Dictionaries claim that the stress on the second syllable is the most common pronunciation in the Caribbean itself, but according to the Dictionary of Caribbean English Usage, the most common pronunciation in <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_English" title="Caribbean English">Caribbean English</a> stresses the first syllable instead, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ær/: 'arr' in 'marry'">ær</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KARR</span>-ih-bee-an</i></a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dce_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-dce-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oed_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-oed-23">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="892" data-file-width="1291" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/300px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/450px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png/600px-CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CIA_map_of_the_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Caribbean</div></div></div>
<p>The word "Caribbean" has multiple uses. Its principal ones are geographical and political. The Caribbean can also be expanded to include territories with strong cultural and historical connections to Africa, <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonisation</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantation_system" title="Plantation system">plantation system</a>.
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_the_Americas" title="United Nations geoscheme for the Americas">United Nations geoscheme for the Americas</a> presents the Caribbean as a distinct region within the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.</li>
<li>Physiographically, the Caribbean region is mainly a chain of islands surrounding the Caribbean Sea. To the north, the region is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Straits_of_Florida" title="Straits of Florida">Straits of Florida</a> and the Northern <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, which lies to the east and northeast. To the south lies the coastline of the continent of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>.</li>
<li>Politically, the "Caribbean" may be centred by considering narrower and wider <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socio-economic" title="Socio-economic">socio-economic</a> groupings:
<ul><li>At its core is the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM), whose full members include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Commonwealth of the Bahamas</a> in the Atlantic, the <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Co-operative Republic of Guyana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Republic of Suriname</a> in South America, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> in Central America; its associate members include <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a> in the Atlantic Ocean.</li>
<li>Most expansive is the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS), which includes almost every nation in the region surrounding the Caribbean and also <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> on the Pacific Ocean. According to the ACS, the total population of its member states is 227 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_and_territories_of_the_Caribbean_today">Countries and territories of the Caribbean today</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Countries and territories of the Caribbean today">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caribbean" title="History of the Caribbean">History of the Caribbean</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="419" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png/220px-Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png/330px-Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_the_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Precolombian languages of the Antilles.<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciboney_Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ciboney Taíno">Ciboney Taíno</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classic_Ta%C3%ADno" title="Classic Taíno">Classic Taíno</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I%C3%B1eri_language" title="Iñeri language">Iñeri</a> were Arawakan, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karina_language" title="Karina language">Karina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yao_language_(Trinidad)" title="Yao language (Trinidad)">Yao</a> were Cariban. <a href="/wiki/Macorix_language" title="Macorix language">Macorix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciguayo_language" title="Ciguayo language">Ciguayo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guanahatabey_language" title="Guanahatabey language">Guanahatabey</a> are unclassified.</div></div></div>
<p>The oldest evidence of humans in the Caribbean is in southern <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> at <a href="/wiki/Banwari_Trace" title="Banwari Trace">Banwari Trace</a>, where remains have been found from seven thousand years ago. These pre-ceramic sites, which belong to the Archaic (pre-ceramic) age, have been termed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ortoiroid" title="Ortoiroid">Ortoiroid</a>. The earliest archaeological evidence of human settlement in <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> dates to about 3600 BC, but the reliability of these finds is questioned. Consistent dates of 3100 BC appear in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. The earliest dates in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a> are from 2000 BC in <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. A lack of pre-ceramic sites in the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> and differences in technology suggest that these Archaic settlers may have Central American origins. Whether an Ortoiroid colonization of the islands took place is uncertain, but there is little evidence of one.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> studies changed some of the traditional beliefs about pre-Columbian indigenous history. According to <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic" title="National Geographic">National Geographic</a>, "studies confirm that a wave of pottery-making farmers—known as Ceramic Age people—set out in canoes from the northeastern coast of South America starting some 2,500 years ago and island-hopped across the Caribbean. They were not, however, the first colonizers. On many islands they encountered a foraging people who arrived some 6,000 or 7,000 years ago...The ceramicists, who are related to today's <a href="/wiki/Arawak_language" title="Arawak language">Arawak</a>-speaking peoples, supplanted the earlier foraging inhabitants—presumably through disease or violence—as they settled new islands."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 400 BC and 200 BC the first ceramic-using agriculturalists, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saladoid_culture" title="Saladoid culture">Saladoid culture</a>, entered Trinidad from South America. They expanded up the Orinoco River to Trinidad, and then spread rapidly up the islands of the Caribbean. Some time after 250 AD another group, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Barancoid&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Barancoid (page does not exist)">Barancoid</a>, entered Trinidad. The Barancoid society collapsed along the Orinoco around 650 AD and another group, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Arauquinoid&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Arauquinoid (page does not exist)">Arauquinoid</a>, expanded into these areas and up the Caribbean chain. Around 1300 AD a new group, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mayoid&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mayoid (page does not exist)">Mayoid</a>, entered Trinidad and remained the dominant culture until Spanish settlement.
</p><p>At the time of the European discovery of most of the islands of the Caribbean, three major Amerindian indigenous peoples lived on the islands: the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Antilles" title="Greater Antilles">Greater Antilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galibi" title="Galibi">Galibi</a> in the Windward Islands, and the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a> in western Cuba. The Taínos are subdivided into Classic Taínos, who occupied Hispaniola and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, Western Taínos, who occupied Cuba, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, and the Bahamian archipelago, and the Eastern Taínos, who occupied the Leeward Islands. Trinidad was inhabited by both Carib speaking and Arawak-speaking groups.
</p><p>Soon after <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> came to the Caribbean, both Portuguese and Spanish explorers began claiming territories in Central and South America. These early colonies brought gold to Europe; most specifically England, the Netherlands, and France. These nations hoped to establish profitable colonies in the Caribbean. Colonial rivalries made the Caribbean a cockpit for European wars for centuries.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_the_Saints,_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3001" data-file-width="4651" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg/220px-The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg/330px-The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg/440px-The_Battle_of_the_Saints%2C_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Battle_of_the_Saints,_12_April_1782_RMG_BHC0444.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Saintes" title="Battle of the Saintes">Battle of the Saintes</a> between British and French fleets in 1782, by <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Pocock" title="Nicholas Pocock">Nicholas Pocock</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Caribbean was known for <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">pirates</a>, especially between 1640 and 1680. The term "<a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">buccaneer</a>" is often used to describe a pirate operating in this region. The Caribbean region was war-torn throughout much of its colonial history, but the wars were often based in Europe, with only minor battles fought in the Caribbean. Some wars, however, were born of political turmoil in the Caribbean itself.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 224px"><div style="width: 224px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 222px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19,_1961._-_panoramio.jpg" title="Counter-attack by Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces supported by T-34 tanks near Playa Giron during the Bay of Pigs Invasion, 19 April 1961"><img alt="Counter-attack by Cuban Revolutionary Armed Forces supported by T-34 tanks near Playa Giron during the Bay of Pigs Invasion, 19 April 1961." data-file-height="693" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg/333px-Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg/500px-Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg/665px-Attack_near_Playa_Giron._April_19%2C_1961._-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="222"/></a></div></div>
<div class="gallerytext">

</div></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_interventions_by_Cuba">Foreign interventions by Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign interventions by Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_interventions_by_Cuba" title="Foreign interventions by Cuba">Foreign interventions by Cuba</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-Off_topic plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may contain material <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Guide_to_writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Guide to writing better articles">unrelated or insufficiently related to the topic of the article</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> or discuss this issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Caribbean" title="Talk:Caribbean">talk page</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="579" data-file-width="616" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/220px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/330px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG/440px-Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cuban_PT-76_Angola.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Cuban <a href="/wiki/PT-76" title="PT-76">PT-76</a> tank crew performing routine security duties in Angola during the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_intervention_in_Angola" title="Cuban intervention in Angola">Cuban intervention into the country</a></div></div></div>
<p>From 1966 until the late 1980s, the Soviet government upgraded Cuba's military capabilities, and Cuban leader <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> saw to it that Cuba assisted with the independence struggles of several countries across the world, most notably <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> in southern Africa, and the anti-imperialist struggles of countries such as Syria, Algeria, Venezuela, Bolivia, and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-35">[33]</a></sup> Its Angolan involvement was particularly intense and noteworthy with heavy assistance given to the Marxist–Leninist <a href="/wiki/MPLA" title="MPLA">MPLA</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>. Cuba sent 380,000 troops to Angola and 70,000 additional civilian technicians and volunteers. (The Cuban forces possessed 1,000 tanks, 600 armored vehicles and 1,600 artillery pieces.)
</p><p>Cuba's involvement in the Angolan Civil War began in the 1960s, when relations were established with the leftist Movement for the Popular Liberation of Angola (MPLA). The MPLA was one of three organizations struggling to gain Angola's independence from Portugal, the other two being <a href="/wiki/UNITA" title="UNITA">UNITA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_of_Angola" title="National Liberation Front of Angola">National Liberation Front of Angola</a> (FNLA). In August and October 1975, the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Defence_Force" title="South African Defence Force">South African Defence Force</a> (SADF) intervened in Angola in support of the UNITA and FNLA. On 14 October 1975, the SADF commenced <a href="/wiki/Operation_Savannah_(Angola)" title="Operation Savannah (Angola)">Operation Savannah</a> in an effort to capture Luanda from the south. On 5 November 1975, without consulting Moscow, the Cuban government opted for a direct intervention with combat troops (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Carlota" title="Operation Carlota">Operation Carlota</a>) in support of the MPLA and the combined MPLA-Cuban armies managed to stop the South African advance by 26 November.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Ogaden_War" title="Ogaden War">Ogaden War</a> (1977–78) in which Somalia attempted to invade an Ethiopia affected by civil war, Cuba deployed 18,000 troops along with armored vehicles, artillery, <a href="/wiki/T-62" title="T-62">T-62</a> tanks, and MiGs to assist the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_Military_Government_of_Socialist_Ethiopia" title="Provisional Military Government of Socialist Ethiopia">Provisional Military Government of Socialist Ethiopia</a>. Cuban troops and warplanes played a major part in the expulsion of Somali regulars from the Ogaden.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_interventions">US interventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: US interventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_interventions_by_the_United_States" title="Foreign interventions by the United States">Foreign interventions by the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_imperialism" title="American imperialism">American imperialism</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> has conducted military operations in the Caribbean for at least 100 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>, the United States gained a major influence on most Caribbean nations. In the early part of the 20th century this influence was extended by participation in the <a href="/wiki/Banana_Wars" title="Banana Wars">Banana Wars</a>. Victory in the Spanish–American War and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Platt_Amendment" title="Platt Amendment">Platt Amendment</a> in 1901 ensured that the United States would have the right to interfere in Cuban political and economic affairs, militarily if necessary. After the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a> of 1959, relations deteriorated rapidly leading to the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>, and successive US attempts to destabilize the island, based upon <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> fears of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet" title="Soviet">Soviet</a> threat. The US invaded and occupied Hispaniola for 19 years (1915–34), subsequently dominating the Haitian economy through aid and loan repayments. The US invaded Haiti again <a href="/wiki/Operation_Uphold_Democracy" title="Operation Uphold Democracy">in 1994</a> and in 2004 were accused by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CARICOM" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a> of arranging a <a href="/wiki/2004_Haitian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2004 Haitian coup d'état">coup d'état</a> to remove elected Haitian leader Jean-Bertrand Aristide. In 1965, 23,000 US troops were sent to the Dominican Republic to quash a local uprising against military rule (see <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Civil_War" title="Dominican Civil War">Dominican Civil War</a>). President Lyndon Johnson had ordered the invasion to stem what he deemed to be a "Communist threat." However, the mission appeared ambiguous and was roundly condemned throughout the hemisphere as a return to <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">gunboat diplomacy</a>. In 1983, the US <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Grenada" title="United States invasion of Grenada">invaded Grenada</a> to remove populist left-wing leader Maurice Bishop. The US maintains a naval military base in Cuba at <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">Guantanamo Bay</a>. The base is one of five unified commands whose "area of responsibility" is <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and the Caribbean. The command is headquartered in Miami, Florida.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/220px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/330px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png/440px-Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tectonic_plates_Caribbean.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FAD4AF; color:black;"> </span> The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Plate" title="Caribbean Plate">Caribbean Plate</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>The geography and climate in the Caribbean region varies: Some islands in the region have relatively flat terrain of non-volcanic origin. These islands include <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> (possessing only minor volcanic features), <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">the Bahamas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>. Others possess rugged towering mountain-ranges like the islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin_(island)" title="Saint Martin (island)">Saint Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba_(island)" title="Saba (island)">Saba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_U.S._Virgin_Islands" title="Saint John, U.S. Virgin Islands">Saint John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>.
</p><p>Definitions of the terms Greater Antilles and Lesser Antilles often vary. The Virgin Islands as part of the Puerto Rican bank are sometimes included with the Greater Antilles. The term Lesser Antilles is often used to define an island arc that includes Grenada but excludes Trinidad and Tobago and the Leeward Antilles.
</p><p>The waters of the Caribbean Sea host large, migratory schools of fish, turtles, and <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> formations. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Trench" title="Puerto Rico Trench">Puerto Rico Trench</a>, located on the fringe of the Atlantic Ocean and Caribbean Sea just to the north of the island of Puerto Rico, is the deepest point in all of the Atlantic Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>The region sits in the line of several major shipping routes with the <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">Panama Canal</a> connecting the western Caribbean Sea with the Pacific Ocean.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johny_Cay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2674" data-file-width="4019" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/220px-Johny_Cay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/330px-Johny_Cay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Johny_Cay.jpg/440px-Johny_Cay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johny_Cay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tropical monsoon climate in <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_(island)" title="San Andrés (island)">San Andrés island</a>, Caribbean, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1609" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Caribbean_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate</a> map of the islands of the Caribbean.</div></div></div>
<p>The climate of the area is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">tropical</a>, varying from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate" title="Tropical rainforest climate">tropical rainforest</a> in some areas to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna</a> in others. There are also some locations that are <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> climates with considerable drought in some years, and the peaks of mountains tend to have cooler <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climates</a>.
</p><p>Rainfall varies with elevation, size and water currents, such as the cool upwellings that keep the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> arid. Warm, moist <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> blow consistently from the east, creating both rain forest and semi arid climates across the region. The tropical rainforest climates include lowland areas near the Caribbean Sea from <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> north to <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, while the more seasonal dry tropical savanna climates are found in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, northern  <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, and southern <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán, Mexico</a>. Arid climates are found along the extreme northern coast of Venezuela out to the islands including <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Curacao" title="Curacao">Curacao</a>, as well as the northwestern tip of Yucatán.
</p><p>While the region generally is sunny much of the year, the wet season from May through November sees more frequent cloud cover (both broken and overcast), while the dry season from December through April is more often clear to mostly sunny. Seasonal rainfall is divided into 'dry' and 'wet' seasons, with the latter six months of the year being wetter than the first half. The air temperature is hot much of the year, varying from 25 to 33 C (77 F to 90 F) between the wet and dry seasons. Seasonally, monthly mean temperatures vary from only about 5 C (7 F) in the northern most regions, to less than 3 C  in the southernmost areas of the Caribbean.
</p><p>Hurricane season is from June to November, but they occur more frequently in August and September and more common in the northern islands of the Caribbean. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Hurricane_or_typhoon" title="Tropical cyclone">Hurricanes</a> that sometimes batter the region usually strike northwards of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> and to the west of Barbados. The principal hurricane belt arcs to northwest of the island of Barbados in the Eastern Caribbean. A great example being recent events of Hurricane Irma devastating the island of Saint Martin during the 2017 hurricane season.
</p><p>Sea surface temperatures change little annually, normally running from 30 °C (87 °F) in the warmest months to 26 °C (76 °F) in the coolest months. The air temperature is warm year round, in the 70s, 80s and 90s, and only varies from winter to summer about 2–5 degrees on the southern islands and about a 10–20 degrees difference on the northern islands of the Caribbean. The northern islands, like the Bahamas, Cuba, Puerto Rico and the Dominican Republic, may be influenced by continental masses during winter months, such as cold fronts.
</p><p><b>Aruba: Latitude 12°N</b>
</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1085" data-file-width="1861" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/220px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/330px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG/440px-Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caribbean_spanish_names.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The mostly Spanish-controlled Caribbean in the 16th century</div></div></div>
<p>All islands at some point were, and a few still are, <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colonies</a> of European nations; a few are <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">overseas or dependent territories</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone Caribbean</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> (from 1797) and the <a href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos_Islands" title="Turks and Caicos Islands">Turks and Caicos Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Danish_West_Indies" title="Danish West Indies">Danish West Indies</a></b> – Possession of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denmark-Norway" title="Denmark-Norway">Denmark-Norway</a> before <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_Constitution" title="Norwegian Constitution">1814</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, present-day <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_West_Indies" title="Dutch West Indies">Dutch West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba_(island)" title="Saba (island)">Saba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Surinam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>), <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Kitts" title="St. Kitts">St. Kitts</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (briefly), <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a>, the current French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement_d%27outre-mer" title="Département d'outre-mer">overseas <i>départements</i></a> of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Marie-Galante" title="Marie-Galante">Marie-Galante</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Les_Saintes" title="Les Saintes">Les Saintes</a>), the current French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivit%C3%A9_d%27outre-mer" title="Collectivité d'outre-mer">overseas collectivities</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_Saint_Martin" title="Collectivity of Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese West Indies</a></b> – present-day <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, known as <i><span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">Os Barbados</i></span></i> in the 16th century when the Portuguese claimed the island en route to Brazil. The Portuguese left Barbados abandoned years before the British arrived.</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>), <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> (until 1659, lost to France), <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> (until 1655, lost to Great Britain), the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a> (until 1670 to Great Britain) <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> (until 1797, lost to Great Britain) and <a href="/wiki/Bay_Islands_Department" title="Bay Islands Department">Bay Islands</a> (until 1643, lost to Great Britain), coastal islands of <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a> (except Belize), and some Caribbean coastal islands of <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.</li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_West_Indies" title="Swedish West Indies">Swedish West Indies</a></b> – present-day French <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint-Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint-Barthélemy">Saint-Barthélemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (briefly) and <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (briefly).</li>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Courland_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Courland colonization of the Americas">Courlander West Indies</a></b> – <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> (until 1691)</li></ul>
<p>The British West Indies were united by the United Kingdom into a <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> between 1958 and 1962. The independent countries formerly part of the B.W.I. still have a joint <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> team that competes in <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test matches</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day Internationals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 Internationals</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Indian_cricket_team" title="West Indian cricket team">West Indian cricket team</a> includes the South American nation of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, the only former British colony on the mainland of that continent.
</p><p>In addition, these countries share the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> as a regional entity. The university consists of three main campuses in Jamaica, Barbados and Trinidad and Tobago, a smaller campus in the Bahamas and Resident Tutors in other contributing territories such as Trinidad.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Caribbean islands have one of the most diverse eco systems in the world. The animals, fungi and plants, and have been classified as one of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">biodiversity hotspots</a> because of their exceptionally diverse terrestrial and marine ecosystems, ranging from montane <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cloud_forests" title="Cloud forests">cloud forests</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a>,  to <a href="/wiki/Cactus" title="Cactus">cactus</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scrubland" title="Scrubland">scrublands</a>. The region also contains about 8% (by surface area) of the world's coral reefs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> along with extensive seagrass meadows,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> both of which are frequently found in the shallow marine waters bordering the island and continental coasts of the region.
</p><p>For the fungi, there is a modern checklist based on nearly 90,000 records derived from specimens in reference collections, published accounts and field observations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> That checklist includes more than 11,250 species of fungi recorded from the region. As its authors note, the work is far from exhaustive, and it is likely that the true total number of fungal species already known from the Caribbean is higher. The true total number of fungal species occurring in the Caribbean, including species not yet recorded, is likely far higher given the generally accepted estimate that only about 7% of all fungi worldwide have been discovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[44]</a></sup> Though the amount of available information is still small, a first effort has been made to estimate the number of fungal species endemic to some Caribbean islands. For Cuba, 2200 species of fungi have been tentatively identified as possible endemics of the island;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the number is 789 species;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, the number is 699 species;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup> for Trinidad and Tobago, the number is 407 species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of the <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a> of the Caribbean islands have been devastated by <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>, pollution, and human encroachment. The arrival of the first humans is correlated with extinction of <a href="/wiki/Tyto_pollens" title="Tyto pollens">giant</a> <a href="/wiki/Ornimegalonyx" title="Ornimegalonyx">owls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megalocnus" title="Megalocnus">dwarf ground sloths</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> The hotspot contains dozens of highly threatened animals (ranging from birds, to mammals and reptiles), fungi and plants. Examples of threatened animals include the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_amazon" title="Puerto Rican amazon">Puerto Rican amazon</a>, two species of <a href="/wiki/Solenodon" title="Solenodon">solenodon</a> (giant shrews) in Cuba and the Hispaniola island, and the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_crocodile" title="Cuban crocodile">Cuban crocodile</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:758px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isla_Saona.jpg" title="Saona Island, Dominican Republic"><img alt="" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="3173" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/750px-Isla_Saona.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/1125px-Isla_Saona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Isla_Saona.jpg/1500px-Isla_Saona.jpg 2x" width="750"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Isla_Saona.jpg" title="File:Isla Saona.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Saona_Island" title="Saona Island">Saona Island</a>, Dominican Republic</div></div></div>
<p>The region's coral reefs, which contain about 70 species of hard corals and between 500–700 species of reef-associated fishes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> have undergone rapid decline in ecosystem integrity in recent years, and are considered particularly vulnerable to global warming and ocean acidification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> According to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNEP" title="UNEP">UNEP</a> report, the Caribbean coral reefs might get extinct in next 20 years due to population explosion along the coast lines, overfishing, the pollution of coastal areas and global warming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Caribbean islands have terrain that Europeans found suitable for cultivation for agriculture. <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">Tobacco</a> was an important early crop during the colonial era, but was eventually overtaken by <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> production as the region's staple crop. Sugar was produced from sugarcane for export to Europe. <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> were historically the largest producers of <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>. The tropical plantation system thus came to dominate Caribbean settlement.  Other islands were found to have terrain unsuited for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, for example <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, which remains heavily forested. The islands in the southern <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, are extremely arid, making them unsuitable for agriculture. However, they have <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a> pans that were exploited by the Dutch. Sea water was pumped into shallow ponds, producing coarse salt when the water evaporated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The natural environmental diversity of the Caribbean islands has led to recent growth in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eco-tourism" title="Eco-tourism">eco-tourism</a>. This type of tourism is growing on islands lacking sandy beaches and dense human populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants_and_animals">Plants and animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Plants and animals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_groups">Indigenous groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Indigenous groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
